     132             : #define DEFAULT_LEARNING_MIN_SEQUENTIAL 4
     133             : /*!
     134             :  * \brief Calculate the min learning duration in ms.
     135             :  *
     136             :  * \details
     137             :  * The min supported packet size represents 10 ms and we need to account
     138             :  * for some jitter and fast clocks while learning.  Some messed up devices
     139             :  * have very bad jitter for a small packet sample size.  Jitter can also
     140             :  * be introduced by the network itself.
     141             :  *
     142             :  * So we'll allow packets to come in every 9ms on average for fast clocking
     143             :  * with the last one coming in 5ms early for jitter.
     144             :  */
     145             : #define CALC_LEARNING_MIN_DURATION(count) (((count) - 1) * 9 - 5)
     146             : #define DEFAULT_LEARNING_MIN_DURATION CALC_LEARNING_MIN_DURATION(DEFAULT_LEARNING_MIN_SEQUENTIAL)

    4016             :          * Convert usec to 0.32 bit fixed point without overflow.
    4017             :          *
    4018             :          * = usec * 2^32 / 10^6
    4019             :          * = usec * 2^32 / (2^6 * 5^6)

    5148           0 : static struct ast_frame *process_dtmf_cisco(struct ast_rtp_instance *instance, unsigned char *data, int len, unsigned int seqno, unsigned int timestamp, int payloadtype, int mark)

    5150           0 :         struct ast_rtp *rtp = ast_rtp_instance_get_data(instance);
    5151             :         unsigned int event, flags, power;
    5152           0 :         char resp = 0;
    5153             :         unsigned char seq;
    5154           0 :         struct ast_frame *f = NULL;
    5155             : 
    5156           0 :         if (len < 4) {
    5157           0 :                 return NULL;
    5158             :         }
    5159             : 
    5160             :         /*      The format of Cisco RTP DTMF packet looks like next:
    5161             :                 +0                              - sequence number of DTMF RTP packet (begins from 1,
    5162             :                                                   wrapped to 0)
    5163             :                 +1                              - set of flags
    5164             :                 +1 (bit 0)              - flaps by different DTMF digits delimited by audio
    5165             :                                                   or repeated digit without audio???
    5166             :                 +2 (+4,+6,...)  - power level? (rises from 0 to 32 at begin of tone
    5167             :                                                   then falls to 0 at its end)
    5168             :                 +3 (+5,+7,...)  - detected DTMF digit (0..9,*,#,A-D,...)
    5169             :                 Repeated DTMF information (bytes 4/5, 6/7) is history shifted right
    5170             :                 by each new packet and thus provides some redudancy.
    5171             : 
    5172             :                 Sample of Cisco RTP DTMF packet is (all data in hex):
    5173             :                         19 07 00 02 12 02 20 02
    5174             :                 showing end of DTMF digit '2'.
    5175             : 
    5176             :                 The packets
    5177             :                         27 07 00 02 0A 02 20 02
    5178             :                         28 06 20 02 00 02 0A 02
    5179             :                 shows begin of new digit '2' with very short pause (20 ms) after
    5180             :                 previous digit '2'. Bit +1.0 flips at begin of new digit.
    5181             : 
    5182             :                 Cisco RTP DTMF packets comes as replacement of audio RTP packets
    5183             :                 so its uses the same sequencing and timestamping rules as replaced
    5184             :                 audio packets. Repeat interval of DTMF packets is 20 ms and not rely
    5185             :                 on audio framing parameters. Marker bit isn't used within stream of
    5186             :                 DTMFs nor audio stream coming immediately after DTMF stream. Timestamps
    5187             :                 are not sequential at borders between DTMF and audio streams,
    5188             :         */
    5189             :

    6680             :                 /*
    6681             :                  * Scenario setup:
    6682             :                  * PartyA -- Ast1 -- Ast2 -- PartyB
    6683             :                  *
    6684             :                  * The learning timeout is necessary for Ast1 to handle the above
    6685             :                  * setup where PartyA calls PartyB and Ast2 initiates direct media
    6686             :                  * between Ast1 and PartyB.  Ast1 may lock onto the Ast2 stream and
    6687             :                  * never learn the PartyB stream when it starts.  The timeout makes
    6688             :                  * Ast1 stay in the learning state long enough to see and learn the
    6689             :                  * RTP stream from PartyB.
    6690             :                  *
    6691             :                  * To mitigate against attack, the learning state cannot switch
    6692             :                  * streams while there are competing streams.  The competing streams
    6693             :                  * interfere with each other's qualification.  Once we accept a
    6694             :                  * stream and reach the timeout, an attacker cannot interfere
    6695             :                  * anymore.
    6696             :                  *
    6697             :                  * Here are a few scenarios and each one assumes that the streams
    6698             :                  * are continuous:
    6699             :                  *
    6700             :                  * 1) We already have a known stream source address and the known
    6701             :                  * stream wants to change to a new source address.  An attacking
    6702             :                  * stream will block learning the new stream source.  After the
    6703             :                  * timeout we re-lock onto the original stream source address which
    6704             :                  * likely went away.  The result is one way audio.
    6705             :                  *
    6706             :                  * 2) We already have a known stream source address and the known
    6707             :                  * stream doesn't want to change source addresses.  An attacking
    6708             :                  * stream will not be able to replace the known stream.  After the
    6709             :                  * timeout we re-lock onto the known stream.  The call is not
    6710             :                  * affected.
    6711             :                  *
    6712             :                  * 3) We don't have a known stream source address.  This presumably
    6713             :                  * is the start of a call.  Competing streams will result in staying
    6714             :                  * in learning mode until a stream becomes the victor and we reach
    6715             :                  * the timeout.  We cannot exit learning if we have no known stream
    6716             :                  * to lock onto.  The result is one way audio until there is a victor.
    6717             :                  *
    6718             :                  * If we learn a stream source address before the timeout we will be
    6719             :                  * in scenario 1) or 2) when a competing stream starts.
    6720             :                  */
